The New Draft of the Four-Power Pact Has Been Sent by the Italian Government to Geneva. The American Representative Agrees to Sign It Immediately. 51

(London) Political circles in London have verified that the new draft of the Four-Power Pact proposed by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini has been agreed upon by the Italian government and the French and British ambassadors and Prussian Prime Minister Goering stationed in Rome. The original draft has been greatly changed. The new draft has been sent by the Italian government to Geneva. The British Foreign Secretary and the French and German Foreign Ministers will gather there within days to discuss it. Most believe that the signing of this pact depends on whether the American representative to the Disarmament Conference, Davis, agrees or not. (Reuters, 22nd) (Berlin) Political circles in Berlin earnestly stated that the talks in Rome have indeed given hope for the early conclusion of the Four-Power Pact, but these talks have not yet been completed. The ambassadors of the major powers concerned have been invited to the Italian Ministry of Foreign Affairs tonight to discuss unresolved issues. Although a compromise has been reached, it is only a draft and must now be discussed by the foreign affairs authorities of the major powers in Geneva. (Reuters, 22nd)

(Nanjing) According to diplomatic sources, the situation in Europe has shown progress recently. The draft Four-Power Pact proposed by the Italian Prime Minister has been fully agreed upon and accepted by Britain, France, Germany, and Italy. This pact can guarantee the security of Europe. As for the Disarmament Conference, since Roosevelt made the application, it has broken the depressed situation. Recently, the American representative Davis made a strong statement on the peace application of the American President at the Disarmament Conference. The future trend of disarmament is likely to accept the recommendations of British Prime Minister MacDonald. Only after considerable success and internal unity in Europe can the situation in the Far East be dealt with. The US President's proposal to conclude a non-aggression pact can also be realized. Yesterday, members of the Labour Party in the British House of Commons questioned the government on whether it would continue to remain silent on Japan's invasion of China. MacDonald firmly denied it. From this, it can be seen that the Far East issue will not be ignored by the European authorities. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

Contents of the Four-Power Pact 52

(Paris) The Four-Power Pact of Britain, France, Germany, and Italy has been revised, and all points have been agreed upon. However, Articles 2 and 3 of the five preambles have not been completely finalized. The basis of this agreement is the Covenant of the League of Nations, the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and the Locarno Treaty. Article 1 stipulates that all matters must be done within the structure of the League of Nations. The four countries must work together within this structure to organize peace. Article 2 speaks of Germany's demands for equality, emphasizes Articles 10 and 9 of the Covenant of the League of Nations, and reiterates the declaration of December 10. Article 3 emphasizes the necessity of the four countries adopting a common policy within the possible scope. Article 4 states the effective period of this pact, approximately ten years. Article 5 stipulates that this pact must be approved by the League of Nations. (Reuters, 23rd)

Remarks of the U.S. Representative at the Disarmament Conference 53

Diverse Reactions from Various Countries; British Press Sees a Change in Traditional U.S. Policy

French Press Says the Guarantees Provided by Davis are Inadequate; Germans Claim Germany's Equal Rights are Already Established

U.S. Press Points to Further Recommendations from Roosevelt

(London) The British press today welcomes the remarks of the U.S. representative, Davis, in

Geneva, considering them a practical explanation and supplement to President Roosevelt's declaration, indicating to some extent that the United States has abandoned neutrality. The Times comments on the change in the traditional U.S. policy regarding neutrality and freedom of the seas, stating that this is a crucial moment and a great success has already been achieved. It anticipates that international control of armaments will soon be victorious. The Daily Telegraph calls Davis's announcement a reassurance, and the Daily Express says it is a promise by the United States to support the League of Nations in implementing sanctions under the League Covenant. The Westminster Gazette says that events have moved a step further, with the United States formally promising to actively safeguard world peace. The Daily Mail points to this as another indication of U.S. readiness to participate in peacekeeping efforts. The least enthusiastic among the British newspapers are the Morning Post and the Daily Sketch. The Morning Post says that what Davis has agreed to is, at most, a slight nod of approval to those who are in the right. The Daily Sketch says that to claim that the U.S. proposal can bring peace closer is simply deceiving people. (Reuters, 23rd)

(Berlin) Dr. Wiesenburg, who recently served as Hitler's

special envoy to England, published an article in a German newspaper today praising U.S. representative Davis, saying that Davis has made the world understand the essence of Germany's position: that disarmament is the path to peace, and that Germany's equal rights have been effectively established. The German press's criticism of Davis's speech in Geneva yesterday is generally similar in tone. (Reuters, 23rd)

(Paris) Most French newspapers do not criticize U.S.

representative Davis's speech in Geneva yesterday. The general consensus is that France will not abandon substance for illusion, and will not reduce armaments until France has sufficient guarantees. The guarantees given by Davis are still inadequate. (Reuters, 23rd)

(New York) U.S. public opinion's criticism of Davis's

Geneva speech points to a step beyond President Roosevelt's recommendations. The New York Times says that the U.S. attitude has now changed publicly, as it now advances and retreats with the world, and can no longer pride itself on being uninvolved. Washington dispatches in various New York newspapers all say that Davis's remarks indicate that the U.S. is now abandoning its traditional policy of neutrality and freedom of the seas. (Reuters, 23rd)

(Washington) Democratic leader Senator Lewis, who has

long opposed U.S. involvement in European disputes, now fully supports Davis's statements in Geneva today. Secretary of State Hull hopes that Davis's remarks will lead to the early success of the disarmament conference, but hopes that the United States will retain its freedom of decision. (Reuters, 22nd)

U.S.-France Dispute on Agenda 54

Minor Setback at Disarmament Conference

Five-Power Meeting Decides on Procedures

(Geneva) When the meeting opened today, the U.S. representative spoke first in a good

atmosphere (his speech was in last night's translation). The British Foreign Secretary followed, expressing the British government's gratitude for Davis's support of disarmament, and saying that he was also grateful for the Italian government's continued support. The British plan was not without its shortcomings, but President Roosevelt's declaration and the German government's statement had completely changed the outlook. The German representative Natolini's remarks that Germany could abolish its armaments, etc., convinced him that detailed discussion of the articles could now begin, and each item could now be put to consideration. French Foreign Minister Poncet took an uncommitted attitude towards the details of the British proposal, as the French government only accepted the British proposal in principle. Poncet declared that the time had come to discuss the political and technical aspects of the disarmament problem, and therefore suggested first discussing the first section of the British draft, especially the issue of regional agreements. The chairman agreed, but U.S. representative Davis opposed this suggestion. (Reuters, 22nd)

(Geneva) A surprising development occurred as the Disarmament Conference's General Committee meeting was coming to

an end, which was quite enough to destroy the harmonious impression created by the previous speeches. After Chairman Henderson agreed that the first section of the British draft would be the starting point for discussion, U.S. representative Davis asked for reconsideration of this procedure, saying that after he had explained the U.S. attitude, it seemed unnecessary to waste time discussing the first section, as the issue of security was more appropriately discussed directly by the countries concerned. This attitude of the U.S. representative was not approved by the French side. France believed that the U.S. representative's insistence was an attempt to force France to be satisfied with the U.S.'s vague and uncertain promise to participate in consultations. Seeing this sudden change, the chairman announced that the General Committee would adjourn until the afternoon of the next day. (Reuters, 22nd) (Geneva) Immediately after the adjournment, Poncet and Davis privately

agreed that the Disarmament General Committee would first begin discussing the Security Convention tomorrow, while private talks would be held on the issue of arms reduction. (National Telegram, 22nd)

(Geneva) After the Disarmament Committee meeting adjourned unhappily today,

it is now scheduled that a meeting of the five major powers of Britain, France, Italy, Germany, and the United States will be held at 11:00 tomorrow morning, at which efforts will be made to agree on the procedures, and then a meeting of the main group will be held to decide on the agenda for the General Committee meeting tomorrow afternoon. (Reuters, 22nd)

(Geneva) The representatives of the five countries, the United States, Germany, Britain, France, and Italy, met at the residence of the chairman of the Disarmament Conference, Henderson, from 10:00 to 12:00 this morning, to decide whether the General Committee should discuss the security issue or the arms issue this afternoon. The debate was quite intense when the representatives of the five countries met. French Foreign Minister Poncet defended France's position, arguing that the arms

reduction that France could commit to depended on mutual security guarantees among countries and international supervision of armaments. Therefore, it was reasonable to start with the security issue. However, most of the representatives requested that the disarmament issue be resolved first. Subsequently, a resolution was passed, declaring that the General Committee should discuss both the disarmament and security issues at the same time, and that no vote should be held on any item before the British plan had its first reading, so that all issues could be considered. (Havas, 23rd)

New Cocoons from Various Places in Zhejiang Come on the Market 79

(Hangzhou) New cocoons from various places in Zhejiang have come on the market, but very few

cocoon brokers have opened their scales, making it difficult for cocoon farmers to sell. Currently, the highest market price for local cocoons is 25 cents per catty, and improved varieties are 35 cents. It is found that local varieties were still sold for 55 cents in 1919 and 40 cents in 1920. The above cocoon prices have fallen year by year, and are now at their lowest. The rural economy is feared to decline further. Currently, the Xiaoshan and Lin'an sericulture model areas have been organized by the Construction Department to form cocoon purchasing committees, raising 700,000 to start purchasing improved cocoons to promote and relieve the situation. (Central News Agency Telegram, 23rd)

Factionalism Gradually Arises Within Japanese Military Leader Araki's Group 80

Masaki Resigns After the Grand Maneuvers; Araki Advocates Simultaneous Invasion of China and Russia

China United Press, Tokyo, 23rd - According to news obtained by this agency's special

correspondent, there have recently been some definite changes in the power dynamics within the Japanese military. Factionalism is gradually arising within Araki's group as well. It is said that the main reason for this is the procedures that should be taken in the future regarding the continental policy after the establishment of "Manchukuo." The views are divided into two types: one is "re-advancing when an opportunity arises," and the other is "advancing at the opportunity." The former is the view of Vice Chief of Staff Masaki, and the latter is the policy of the Kwantung Army. Araki himself leans towards the advancement theory, the details of which are described as follows:

(1) The "Re-Advancement" Advocates Only Eastern Four Provinces, Temporarily Stop

Military Actions, Organize Internal Affairs and Economic Construction in the Eastern Four Provinces. Domestic economic power may not be able to support further expansion of military actions with current domestic economic power. If supplies are cut off, then previous efforts will be in vain. Napoleon and Alexander both failed because they knew how to advance but not how to defend. To build the Eastern Four Provinces, at least ten years of painstaking effort are needed, and international tolerance also has a certain limit. Since ancient times, there have been few who have offended public anger and achieved satisfactory results. Stopping military action and seeking the world's understanding is the right time. The unfinished part of the continental policy can "re-advance when an opportunity arises" in the future. Therefore, this faction is called the "Re-Advancement Theory." Lieutenant General Masaki (Vice Chief of Staff), from Araki's group, is its representative. Ugaki and others mostly support this view. This faction not only does not approve of invading Russia's Maritime Province, but also does not want to invade Pingjin, causing larger-scale resistance. (2) The "Advancement" Advocates Seize This Opportunity, as Russia is Busy with the Second Five-Year Plan, and its military preparations are incomplete. China's internal affairs are not unified, and Europe is in a crisis. While Britain and the United States are taking care of themselves, seize the opportunity to advance again and again, occupying Russia's Maritime Province to the north, seizing North China to the south, and attacking Chahar and Suiyuan to the west. Such a good opportunity given by God, if you don't find a way to use it, when are you waiting for? Invading China only requires 100,000 troops. Collect as many of the Chinese troops who oppose the Central Government as possible to be the vanguard. There is nothing to worry about in the war. The current strength of the Japanese army is enough to defeat the Red Army. As for international issues, it is already isolated in the front, so why fear the back? Therefore, the China Eastern Railway is already under the control of the Japanese army. Why bother negotiating with Russia to buy it back? It can also be considered a great favor to Russia if Japan does not take the opportunity to seize its Maritime Province. Regarding China, we should seize the opportunity to advance until China is disarmed. The representative of this faction is the Kwantung Army, the North China Garrison Army, and the generals in the Army Ministry of the Araki line. The failure of the Seiyukai cabinet and the still bleak prospects for peace in North China are caused by this faction's activities inside and outside. The dispute between the two factions is becoming increasingly fierce. It is reported that Vice Chief of Staff Masaki will therefore be forced to step down. The talk that Lieutenant General Masaki will be promoted to general and resign from his current position after the Grand Maneuvers in August is all an atmosphere created by Araki's direct officers.

Dentsu News Agency, Tokyo, 23rd - Prime Minister Saito, in order

to stabilize the situation, issued the following statement today: "After mature discussions with Finance Minister Takahashi on the 'political situation' issue, Finance Minister Takahashi is willing to continue to dedicate his old body to the country and move forward to overcome difficulties. The current cabinet, in accordance with the decided policy, will work hard on 'Manchukuo,' properly handle relations with China and Russia, and move forward on the path of shaking off the aftermath and refreshing diplomacy, in order to live up to the spirit of the imperial rescript."

Dentsu, Tokyo, 23rd - Thanks to the Finance Minister's remaining, the political situation has been able to stabilize a little. Therefore, it is still questionable whether the Finance Minister has the determination to compile the budget for the next year and attend the parliament. However, since the government knows that the Finance Minister's remaining has been confirmed, it will definitely announce the stabilization of the political situation to the people, and from now on, it will focus its efforts on the implementation of policies.

Gandhi's Condition is Still Good After Two Weeks of Fasting 84

Doctors Marvel at the Inconceivable

Reuters, Pune, 22nd - Gandhi has been fasting for three weeks since May 8th.

Two weeks have now passed. Although his body is very weak, his spirit is still good. His doctors are very surprised, saying that it is almost inconceivable that a person who has been fasting for two weeks can still be so well. It is reported that Gandhi also made a "fast to death" for the sake of the untouchables last September, but after a week, he took nourishment due to the agreement to improve the status of the untouchables. At that time, his body was extremely weak, and the doctors believed that if he fasted for a few more days, his life would be in danger. This time, many devout believers gathered around him, and the famous speaker and poet Mrs. Naidu was also among them.

Page 8

Dispatch from Our Correspondent Geng Ya, Returned from the Front Lines 87

(II) Many Scars of War Seen on the Tianjin-Jinan Train

Outside Tianjin, enemy troops pressed the border; inside, Chinese traitors lurked. Just when rumors were rampant and people were in a state of panic, the northward trip of Mr. Huang Fu brought a breath of relief, reflecting a sense of hope as the clouds seemed to dissipate. However, as Tianjin is close to the coast and located at the intersection of the Beining and Jinpu Railways, the Japanese in North China have been eyeing it covetously, eager to seize it as a base for their operations. Moreover, the Japanese concession, with its garrisoned troops, serves as a breeding ground for all sorts of malfeasance. Consequently, disgruntled warlords, disgraced politicians, and local ruffians, all colluding with the Japanese, are constantly plotting, posing a threat like a thorn in one's side and a worry in one's heart. As the Sino-Japanese problem has evolved to this point, Japan is unwilling to relinquish the Eastern Provinces, and our country cannot sacrifice its territory. Their encirclement and threat to Pingjin (Beiping and Tianjin) is effectively an attempt to force a treaty at the city gates, to acknowledge all their rights and interests in the invasion of Manchuria, which has become a reality. In this kind of situation, akin to riding a tiger, it seems unlikely that Mr. Huang can create a new situation in just two or three days, as if a chronic disease were to meet a miraculous doctor and be cured instantly. On the other hand, there are widespread rumors that the situation will take a surprising turn for the better, with much discussion but no consensus. Due to the rushed schedule, I was unable to stay and quietly observe the events in order to provide readers with a clear and comprehensive report, which I regret deeply. Having decided to return south, I hurried to the Jinpu Railway Station. When the ordinary train arrived, a prisoner was led off the train. He was fat-headed, big-brained, and of impressive build. Following him was a limping wounded soldier, using a crutch for support, cursing and hitting him as he went. When asked what had happened, the answer was that the prisoner was a Chinese traitor who, out of guilt, had behaved suspiciously, leading to interrogation by the police, who found a letter addressed "Respectfully presented to Commander Nakamura." The entire train's passengers kicked and beat him, bringing him close to death. Unexpectedly, once they were off the train, he seemed as energetic as ever. It is said that these heartless Chinese traitors and those who act as accomplices to the enemy receive extremely harsh treatment, earning only forty cents a day and subjected to various restrictions. As soon as a riot order is issued, they are sent to their deaths, yet they only receive one dollar a day. For such a paltry sum, they are willing to sacrifice their lives and harm the country. There is nothing more lamentable than this. The crowding on the train was no less than that on the refugee trains from Beining and Xikai. However, those trains were mostly filled with poor people, while this one had many wealthy merchants and gentry, along with their jewel-bedecked families. This could be seen from the ticket office's announcement that first and second-class tickets were sold out. As the train passed through the main station and the new station (still in Tianjin), many passengers boarded through the windows, struggling to stand upright in the crowd. After several hours of travel, as deep night fell, those who were sitting or lying down snored loudly, while most of those standing were half-asleep, swaying and bumping into each other, leading to occasional arguments. Children, startled awake from their dreams, mumbled to themselves or even kicked, shouted, and cursed, creating a spectacle for the journey. Several people forcibly got off the train, only to realize they had gotten off at the wrong stop. They shouted and got back on, causing the entire train to laugh and startling everyone awake. One energetic man, over forty, said loudly, "The state of China is truly heartbreaking. Years ago, when I traveled from Ping to Jing (Beijing), I sat in a first-class compartment, and my two attendants were also somehow given compartments by the railway bureau. I was shocked, unable to pay such a large fee, but the ticket inspector explained, 'We are under orders to welcome the director' (it is unknown what rank of director the speaker was). 'Please don't be polite; in any case, most of the compartments are empty, and your attendants need not move elsewhere.' From this, you can see how eager the officials are to ingratiate themselves. In my youth, I worked hard to enter the military and political circles, but now I am fortunate to have escaped, though I am scarred and do not want to look back." At that moment, a young woman, reportedly a student from Peking University, struggled to squeeze back to her seat from the toilet, indignant, saying, "There are two villagers squatting on the urine-soaked floor of the toilet. I heard that since the Northeast Incident, they fled from Shenyang to Tangshan to work, but now, because Tangshan has been abandoned, they plan to flee back to their hometown in Shandong. One of them is already sick from the horrors of war and is too weak. So, they are both crammed into the toilet, crying quietly in each other's arms. Although I wanted to advise them not to stay in such an unsanitary place, there was no way to accommodate them on the seats. Some people were sprawled out, occupying the seats of two or three people. When I tried to ask them to give up a seat, they just glared at me. It is lamentable how little empathy the people of this country have." The young woman then saw a baby sleeping soundly on a suitcase, laughing in his sleep. She smiled bitterly, saying, "A baby not even a year old is forced to flee on this bumpy train. I doubt his dreams are good; why is he laughing so heartily?" An old woman sighed in response, "My third grandson looked just like this child. Now, he and his older siblings have become spirits, buried together in a dugout under enemy bombs." As she spoke, tears streamed down her face. When asked, she revealed that she was from Miyun. One morning, enemy planes arrived, and her children and grandchildren rushed into a dugout, where a bomb fell and sealed them inside. Explosions continued nearby, preventing anyone from digging them out, and they all suffocated. She had not yet gotten out of bed and was too terrified to move, which is how she survived. Alone and helpless, she was fleeing to Qufu to seek refuge with relatives. When they arrived in Jinan, passengers got off one after another in large numbers. The reporter took the opportunity to visit Chairman Han but then also got off the train. (19th)

Judgment of the Jiangsu High Court in the Case of Chen Duxiu (Continued) 88

(II) Regarding Wang Wu, namely Song Fengchun, and Pu Yifan:

Defendant Pu Yifan repeatedly denied joining the Communist Party and being elected as an alternate member of the Central Committee of the CCP Opposition. Wang Wu also only admitted to joining the Communist Party in the past and being sentenced to six years' imprisonment by the Shanghai Provisional Military Tribunal in 1931. As for being released on bail during his sentence, re-appointed as an alternate member of the Central Committee of the CCP Opposition, and attending CCP meetings, he denied all of this. However, investigations revealed that the defendants all attended the weekly meetings at the home of co-conspirator Xie Shaoshan and were apprehended along with Peng Shuzhi, Xie Shaoshan, and Wang Zhaoqun. According to Xie Shaoshan's statement to the Shanghai Public Concession Police, "My place is often used for meetings. The standing committee includes five members: Chen Duxiu, Peng Shuzhi, Pu Yifan (namely Bu Dezi), and Luo Shifan and Song Fengchun. The last person was just released from Caohejing Prison and this is the first time they attended a meeting. On the day we were arrested, they were only holding the weekly meeting" (see statement of the Public Concession Police, October 16, 1932). Later, when they were escorted to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, the judge asked, "What kind of organization is your place?" and the answer was, "Our place is an organization led by Trotsky." Asked, "Where do you hold your meetings?" The answer was, "Every Saturday at my house." Asked, "What is Peng Shuzhi's position?" Answer, "He is a standing committee member."

Asked, "What about Pu Yifan and Wang Wu?" Answer, "They are also standing committee members." Asked how many standing committee members there were in total, the answer was "Five in total, all of whom have been apprehended." However, Chen Duxiu is the chairman of the standing committee, Wang Wu only attended for the first time, and I am the secretary of the standing committee" (see minutes of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, October 17, 1932). The prosecutor of this court interrogated Chen Duxiu, who stated that there were three members of the standing committee, himself, Peng Shuzhi, and Zhang Jiu, and the first alternate member was Pu Yifan, and another was either Luo Shifan or Song Fengchun, he couldn't remember clearly. Peng Shuzhi was then interrogated, who also stated that there were three standing committee members, himself, Chen Duxiu, and Zhang Jiu, and the alternate members were Pu Yifan and Song Fengchun (see minutes of the Prosecutor's Office of this court, December 6, 1932). Furthermore, many reactionary documents were found in Pu Yifan's residence at No. 320, Gaofu Lane, Rue Sainte Marie. Song Fengchun had already been expelled from the Third International for his Trotskyist leanings. This time, he was apprehended with Peng Shuzhi at Xie Shaoshan's house. The evidence against him is clear, and there is no room for denial. Although Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi, during the trial in this court, Pu Yifan argued that the alternate standing committee member mentioned earlier at the prosecutor's office was Pu Yifang, not Pu Yifan, and that Pu Yifang's age, appearance, and origin were different from the Pu Yifan who was apprehended. Peng Shuzhi also argued on behalf of Song Fengchun that he had not been released from prison for long and could not have been elected as an alternate standing committee member. The defendants also relied on this counter-evidence to defend themselves. The investigation revealed that Pu Yifang and Pu Yifan have similar pronunciations, but there must first be sufficient evidence to prove that there is another person named Pu Yifang, then the Pu Yifan who is on trial is not an alternate standing committee member, which would be clear even without defense. However, Chen Duxiu and others could not provide evidence that Pu Yifang actually existed, and only because the previous statements were on record, there was no way to deny it and they used the similar sound of the name as a cover. This kind of empty talk is difficult to hide, and only makes the crime more obvious. As for Song Fengchun, although he had not been released from prison for long, Xie Shaoshan's initial statement stated that the last person had just been released from Caohejing Prison and this was the first time they attended a meeting, which is consistent with the facts and with the initial statements of Chen Duxiu and others. Although Xie Shaoshan was not directly questioned by this court, her statements were recorded in the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court and the Public Concession Police Station and can be adopted. As for the defendants' claim that there should be records and a sign-in book for the meetings, the CCP's secret meetings are different from ordinary public meetings and naturally cannot be complete. Moreover, the co-conspirator Xie Shaoshan, who participated in the meeting, testified clearly, so there is no doubt. There is no reason to rely on this as a defense. The above evidence shows that the defendants organized groups and held meetings with the aim of endangering the Republic of China, and the facts are very clear. However, if an alternate standing committee member's actions within the group cannot be proven to have a common intention, they should not be held responsible for other joint crimes.

(III) Regarding Wang Ziping and He Afang:

Defendant Wang Ziping, also known as Zeng Meng, was introduced by his friend Qin Dingyu in 1927 to work as a proofreader at the Chongwentang Printing Press on Jiangwan Road in Shanghai. Later, he was persuaded by Hao Qianzhi, the deputy manager of Chongwentang, to join the Communist Party. Defendant He Afang also joined the Communist Party in February of the same year through an introduction by his friend Jin Muhan, namely Jin Shisheng, and served as a messenger, receiving a monthly salary of twenty yuan. Later, both were expelled from the Third International for opposing the Stalinist faction and joined the CCP Opposition organized by Chen Duxiu and others, and jointly undertook copywriting and printing work within the party. The defendants have repeatedly stated this in their statements. When they were arrested, they were printing "Campus Life" and "Spark" at their residence at No. 335, Yeguang Lane, Tangshan Road. The investigators and the evidence were seized on the spot, so the facts of the crime are very certain. The words propagated in "Campus Life," "Spark," and other publications and leaflets not only fall within the scope of communism but have reached the level of treason. The reasons for this have been explained in detail in the section on Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi. The defendants are members of the CCP Opposition and knew that the documents were used to propagate treason, yet they undertook to print them, so they must bear the responsibility for helping to propagate them, without saying more. However, the defendants were forced by livelihood to seek printing wages. Considering the nature of the crime, they deserve leniency and should be given a reduced sentence.

(IV) Regarding Wang Zhaoqun and Guo Jinghao:

Defendants Wang Zhaoqun and Guo Jinghao have repeatedly denied participating in the CCP Opposition, but Wang Zhaoqun was captured with Peng Shuzhi, Wang Wu, Pu Yifan, Xie Shaoshan, etc., at the home of co-conspirator Xie Shaoshan, and was apprehended while attending the weekly meeting. Xie Shaoshan testified to this, and Xie Shaoshan's house was a secret meeting place for the CCP Opposition, and those who participated in the meetings, such as Peng Shuzhi, Wang Wu, Pu Yifan, etc., were all important people in the organization. If the defendant was not a party member, why would Xie Shaoshan allow him to reside at her residence? Furthermore, Lu Yuanhu, the inspector of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau who cracked the case, stated that Wang Zhaoqun's name was listed as Luo Shifan in the list of CCP members, and that Luo Shifan was a member of the Central Committee of the CCP Opposition. However, Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi insisted that Luo Shifan was another person and not Wang Zhaoqun, and that there were only three members of the standing committee, besides the two of them and Zhang Jiu. After reviewing Xie Shaoshan's statements made during the interrogation by the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court and the Public Concession Police Station, there was no mention of Wang Zhaoqun being Luo Shifan. The list was copied from another list, so it cannot be used as a basis for determining the facts. Although it cannot be proven that Wang Zhaoqun was a member of the standing committee, there is no doubt that he was a member of the CCP Opposition organization as he attended the weekly meetings. Defendant Guo Jinghao, originally named Peng Daozhi, is the brother of Peng Shuzhi and was arrested by the police at Wang Ziping's printing press. Furthermore, the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau seized a school registration form, namely a CCP registration form, which stated that Peng Daozhi joined a group in Changsha, Hunan in September 1925 (1915), and later withdrew informally. In December 1929 (1918), he rejoined the opposition in Shanghai and served as a district committee member and student movement organizer in the Hudong district. He is now in charge of organizational work and student movements in the Huxi district student branch, registered on June 8, 1932. There is also a note "alias Guo Jinghao." Although the words Guo Jinghao have been crossed out, they are still legible, so there is considerable evidence that the defendant joined the CCP Opposition group. However, the defendant is young and ignorant and was lured by his brother Peng Shuzhi, which led to him being caught in the net of the law. The circumstances are excusable, and a reduced sentence should be given.

(V) Regarding Liang Youguang and Wang Jiantang:

The main point of the indictment regarding the defendants' alleged crimes is that their names match the names listed in the CCP communications addresses found at Xie Shaoshan's house, and that many reactionary books were also found in their possession. Furthermore, the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau indicated that Liang Youguang was a provincial inspector of the Chen Duxiu faction. This court reviewed the files of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, which stated that the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau indicated that the defendants were arrested based on the small slips of paper with communication addresses found at Xie Shaoshan's house. However, Lu Yuanhu, the clerk of the bureau who cracked the case, was ordered to appear in court, and testified that there was only one slip of paper found at Xie Shaoshan's house, on which a "Chen" character was written, which was Chen Duxiu's address. There were no other slips of paper with communication addresses, and the defendants were arrested based on Xie Shaoshan's verbal instructions. Therefore, the basis for the defendants' arrest is questionable. Furthermore, this court sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau to inquire about Liang Youguang being a provincial inspector of the Chen Duxiu faction, and they replied that, according to the confession of a self-surrendered person, Xie Shaoshan, the small room at No. 1044 Dongsiwen Lane, Xinzha Road, was the address of Luo Shifan. Luo was the person in charge of organization for the Chen Duxiu faction, so personnel in charge of work in other areas often came to Shanghai to contact Luo and sometimes stayed there. However, Liang Youguang had only been in Shanghai for a short time and had not yet formally met in the organizational relationship. Although the details are not known, he should be a person in charge of work in other areas. Therefore, according to Xie Shaoshan's statement, it was only a conjecture, which is difficult to adopt as a basis. Furthermore, No. 1044 Dongsiwen Lane, Xinzha Road, where Liang Youguang lived, was Luo Shifan's address. Therefore, the name that Xie Shaoshan instructed to arrest at that time should be Luo Shifan, not Liang Youguang, which further proves that the seized books were Luo Shifan's belongings, not Liang Youguang's. Therefore, there is no proof regarding Liang Youguang's criminal acts. As for Liang Youguang's panic and jumping out of the window when the police came to arrest him at night, this alone is difficult to directly indicate that he participated in the Communist Party. Defendant Wang Jiantang stated that he lived at No. 22 Fululi Road and there was more than one family in the house. He was the second landlord, and the books were found in the room of Wang Boping, a tenant in the front building. Because Wang Boping was not in the house, he was brought to the case. It is unclear whether Xie Shaoshan's verbal instructions at the time specifically mentioned Wang Jiantang or Wang Boping. When this court questioned Lu Yuanhu, he stated that he did not remember clearly because it had been a long time. Furthermore, there were eight boxes of documents seized in this case, some related to the study of communism and some unrelated to communism. The ten types of books seized in the house were all mixed with those seized elsewhere when the police sent the case, and the documents did not separately indicate which books came from which location. Therefore, even if the books are considered to belong to Wang Jiantang, it is impossible to prove whether they are books for studying communism, so it is difficult to use this as the only evidence of his joining the Communist Party.

In conclusion, the defendants Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi organized groups with the aim of endangering the Republic of China and used words to propagate treason, thereby committing the crimes in Article 2, Paragraph 2, and Article 6 of the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Crimes Endangering the Republic of China. In accordance with Article 10 of the same law, Article 42 and Article 74 of the Criminal Law, and Article 2, Paragraph 2 of the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Crimes Endangering the Republic of China, and Article 77 of the Criminal Law, they are sentenced to thirteen years of imprisonment and deprived of public rights for fifteen years in accordance with Article 106, Article 56, and Article 57, Paragraph 4 of the Criminal Law. Wang Ziping and He Afang organized groups with the aim of endangering the Republic of China and helped to propagate treason by means of words, in accordance with Article 10 of the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Crimes Endangering the Republic of China, Article 6 and Article 2, Paragraph 2 of the same law, Article 74, Article 44, Paragraph 1, Paragraph 3, First Section, Article 77, Article 78, and Article 87 of the Criminal Law, they are sentenced to five years of imprisonment, with a slight reduction, and deprived of public rights for seven years in accordance with Article 106, Article 56, and Article 57, Paragraph 5 of the Criminal Law. Wang Wu (namely Song Fengchun), Pu Yifan, Wang Zhaoqun, and Guo Jinghao organized groups with the aim of endangering the Republic of China, thereby committing the crime in Article 6 of the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Crimes Endangering the Republic of China. Wang Wu (namely Song Fengchun), Pu Yifan, and Wang Zhaoqun are each sentenced to five years of imprisonment, and Guo Jinghao is sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment in accordance with Article 10 of the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Crimes Endangering the Republic of China and Article 77 of the Criminal Law. Wang Wu, Pu Yifan, and Wang Zhaoqun are each deprived of public rights for seven years, and Guo Jinghao is deprived of public rights for three years, in accordance with Article 106, Article 56, and Article 57, Paragraph 5 of the Criminal Law. The number of days in detention before the judgment is final shall be commuted at a rate of two days of detention for one day of imprisonment in accordance with Article 64 of the Criminal Law. The documents and prohibited books (as per the list in the case file) used for the commission of the crime or in preparation for the crime shall be confiscated in accordance with Article 62, Paragraphs 1 and 2 of the Criminal Law. The criminal suspicion of Liang Youguang and Wang Jiantang cannot be proven, and they are found not guilty in accordance with Article 316 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. The judgment is rendered specifically as stated in the main text.

This case was prosecuted in court by Zhu Jun, the prosecutor of this court, acting in the capacity of prosecutor. The court of appeal for this case is the Supreme Court. If any party is dissatisfied with this judgment, they shall file an appeal with this court within ten days from the day following the delivery of the judgment, in a written statement stating the reasons for dissatisfaction. April 26, 1933, Jiangsu High Court Criminal Second Chamber Presiding Judge Hu Shancheng (seal), Judge Zhang Bingci (seal), Judge Lin Zhezhang (seal). The above is a true copy of the original. Clerk of the Jiangsu High Court, Ding Yi (seal). (End)

The Sichuan War Remains Extremely Fierce 89

Liu Xiang Takes the Opportunity to Deploy Troops to Unify the Sichuan Situation

Chongqing dispatch: After the conflict between Liu and Deng, the entire Sichuan Province has fallen into a state of civil war. Currently, both sides are engaged in fierce battles in Pixian, Xindu, Xinfan, Guanxian, Chongning, and other places. The people are suffering and suffering heavy losses. The latest situation is reported as follows:

The 24th Army Launches a Four-Pronged Attack

At the beginning of the war, Liu Wenhui of the 24th Army immediately appointed Zhang Qingping, the commander of the 1st Division of the army, as the commander of the first route; Leng Nanxun, the commander of the 2nd Division of the Sichuan-Kang Army, as the commander of the second route; Lin Yungen, the commander of the 2nd Division, as the commander of the third route; and Chen Hongwen of the Sichuan-Kang 2nd Division as the commander of the fourth route. Each commander led 12 regiments of men to attack the 28th Army. The allocation of their front lines was as follows: the first route advanced towards Pengxian, Chongning, and Guanxian; the second route advanced towards Pixian and Xinfan; the third route advanced towards Xindu and Jintang; and the fourth route advanced towards Ziyang, Jianyang, and Lezhi. The focus of the battle was on the Pixian and Guanxian areas. On the 13th, the first route launched its attack, and Zhang Qingping's troops engaged in fierce battles with Huang Yin's troops of the 28th Army in Pixian, Guanxian, Chongning, and other places. There was no significant progress on either side. On the 17th, Chen Hongwen's troops of the 24th Army's fourth route advanced towards Ziyang and made contact with Chen Shunong of the 3rd Division of the 28th Army. Chen was unable to resist and retreated step by step. Ziyang was occupied by the 24th Army. Jianyang also fell into the hands of the 24th Army on the 18th. The three counties of Pi, Chong, and Guan were also captured by the 24th Army. During the attack on Pixian on the 18th, fierce battles broke out on both sides, with each side deploying thousands of men to serve as suicide squads, engaging in hand-to-hand combat. In this battle, Zhou Chongsheng, the regimental commander of the 24th Army, was killed in action, and Mao, the regimental commander, and Shi Zhaowu, the brigade commander, were seriously wounded. More than a thousand people died on each side, demonstrating the intensity of the battle. Furthermore, when the 24th Army attacked Chongning on the 17th, fierce battles raged for two days and nights, with more than ten hand-to-hand combats. Zhou Xianpei, the regimental commander of Huang Yin's unit of the 28th Army, was killed in action, and Huang Jianming, the magistrate, was also killed in action. More than 500 houses of residents near Chongcheng were burned, and more than 1,000 people were killed by stray bullets or burned to death. On the 18th, Huang's unit collapsed, and the 24th Army entered the city on the 19th. In the Guanxian area, due to the dangerous terrain and the obstruction of the river, the two sides were deadlocked for seven days, each suffering more than 2,000 casualties. It was not until the 20th that Guanxian was captured by the 24th Army. Currently, the main force is advancing towards Xinfan, Xindu, Jintang, and Huaizhou.

Preparation for the 28th Army's Operations 90

Deng Xihou of the 28th Army, regarding past Sichuan wars, advocated peaceful mediation and was unwilling to escalate the war. When Yuan Zuming, the commander-in-chief of the Guizhou Army, occupied Sichuan, Deng had an actual strength of eighty to ninety thousand men and guns, and controlled three-fifths of Sichuan. Since the Jinggangshan Meeting, Deng had voluntarily ceded more than thirty counties for allied forces to garrison. Last year, the 21st and 24th Armies became hostile, and he maintained neutrality. After Liu Wenhui of the 24th Army returned to Chengdu, various misunderstandings arose, and there were rumors that Liu intended to eliminate the 28th Army. Deng initially dismissed this, but later, responsible persons from the 24th Army openly expressed such intentions, and Deng began to flee the province in a panic, under the pretext of assembling troops to assist Tian Songyao in suppressing bandits, but in reality, he was actively preparing for military action. In the Xindu area, he convened a meeting of all the army's generals, and decided on three operational steps: (1) Completely concentrate all units of the army in Xindu, Jintang, and Guanghan counties, and decide on a counter-offensive plan after completing contact with all parties. (2) Completely transfer the troops in Chengdu, sacrificing all provincial institutions and ceding them to the 24th Army to avoid street fighting in the provincial capital, which would cause suffering to the people and be criticized by all parties. (3) Unite with the 29th Army for mutual survival and destruction, and unite with Liu Xiang of the 21st Army, Li Jiayu of the New 6th Division, and Luo Zezhou of the 23rd Division to jointly attack the 24th Army and fundamentally resolve the issue. If advancing is impossible, retreat entirely into Songpan, Maowen, and Maoxian to plan for a future resurgence. After the above methods were decided, the various armies of the 28th Army became determined to fight to the death against the 24th Army. Therefore, the 28th Army, which had been regarded as weak by various armies in Sichuan for many years, has now changed its past attitude and repeatedly defeated the brave troops of the 24th Army, such as Li Yushu and Shi Zhaowu.

Recent General Situation of the Sichuan War 91

Currently, the 28th and 24th Armies are in a stalemate in the Xindu, Xinfan, and Huaizhou areas. Both sides have entered a period of major warfare. Deng Xihou has personally gone to the front line to command military affairs, and Liu Wenhui also left the province on the 20th to inspect the positions.

In order to concentrate his forces, Liu Xihou specifically ordered Chen Shunong's division and Xie Decan to abandon Ziyang, Jianyang, and Lezhi counties, and transfer all of them to Xindu and Guanghan. As for Ziyang, Jianyang, and Lezhi counties, except for Lezhi, which has not been occupied by Liu Wenhui's troops, Ziyang and Jianyang have already fallen within the scope of the 24th Army. Deng, in order to do a favor, specifically ceded the three counties of Ziyang, Jianyang, and Lezhi to Li Jiayu of the New 6th Division and Luo Zezhou of the 23rd Division (both of which were formerly under Deng). Currently, Lezhi has been taken over by Li's troops. As for Ziyang and Jianyang, Li has also sent three brigades to take over the defense. Chen Hongwen's troops of the 24th Army did not participate in this matter, leading to conflict. In Beidouzhen, Jinjiazai, and other places, the New 6th Division opened fire on the 24th Army on the 19th, resulting in fierce fighting. At the same time, Tian Songyao of the 29th Army, who was busy suppressing the Red bandits, was deeply afraid that if the lips are gone, the teeth will be cold, endangering his army. Therefore, he has currently stopped the bandit suppression mission and sent the army's Deputy Commander Sun Zhen, leading the 2nd Division (Zeng Nanfu) and the entire 4th Division (Wang Mingzhang), to concentrate in Deyang and assist the 28th Army. Sun Deshao, in order to seek peace and resolve the Sichuan war, specifically sent Major General Chief of Staff Ma Yaozhen to the province to meet with Liu Wenhui of the 24th Army, requesting that military action be stopped and to await a solution from the central government, but he did not receive a satisfactory reply. Sun immediately ordered mobilization, and the brave soldiers of the two divisions have successively joined the 28th Army's front lines to fight, and the scope of the war has expanded.

Liu Xiang Sends Troops to Unify the Sichuan Situation 92

Since Liu Xiang of the 21st Army defeated his uncle Liu Wenhui last year, his strength has greatly increased for a time. He now has as many as 130,000 to 140,000 elite troops, and occupying the rich southeastern region of Sichuan, he inevitably has a sense of pride and is constantly preparing to unify the Sichuan situation, but he has not yet had an opportunity. Now that Liu Wenhui and Deng Xihou have started a war, and Deng's strength is not as good as that of the 24th Army, he sent representatives Xie Decan (brigade commander of the 5th Mixed Brigade of the 28th Army) and Kou Chengbo (chief of the Quartermaster Department of the 28th Army) to Chongqing to meet with Liu Xiang, requesting that he send troops to quell the chaos and jointly pacify the 24th Army and unify the Sichuan situation. Liu Xiang believes that this issue is of great importance and is not convenient to act rashly. He sent telegrams to Deng Xihou, Tian Songyao, Yang Sen, and Liu Cunhou to solicit their opinions. Deng, Tian, Yang, and others replied in telegrams, all expressing extreme approval and unanimously supporting Mr. Fu to unify Sichuan. Liu was overjoyed at this opportunity and issued a mobilization order yesterday, appointing Pan Wenying of the entire teaching division, Jian Hu of the model division, Wang Zejun of the 2nd Division, and Fan Shaozeng of the 4th Division to advance towards Jianwei, Jiading, Jingyan, and Renshou in four directions to take over the defense areas of the 24th Army, and appointed Pan Wenying as the commander-in-chief of the front and Guo Xunwen as the deputy commander to command the various troops to proceed. According to yesterday evening's telegram, the 21st and 24th Armies have already begun fighting in Jingyan and Renshou, and the scope of the war has further expanded. This is Liu Xiang's battle to unify the Sichuan situation. However, whether the fragmented Sichuan situation can be unified by Liu Xiang, we will wait and see. (22nd)

Opposition from Merchants and People in the Old Chuzhou Prefecture, Zhejiang Province, to Highway Share Payments 93

Hangzhou News: The old Chuzhou Prefecture in Zhejiang Province, including Suichang, Songyang, Longquan, Xuanping, Qingtian, Yunhe, Jinyun, Jingning, Qingyuan, and other eleven counties, has many mountains and little farmland, and is rich in forests, bamboo, and wood products, which are sold to Shanghai, Hangzhou, Wenzhou, and Japan. However, in recent years, Russian pine has been dumped, wood prices have plummeted, economic relations between China and Japan have been severed, the charcoal industry has gone bankrupt, and the bamboo and wood industry has stagnated due to the decline of the fishing industry. The entire bamboo, wood, and charcoal industry in the old Chuzhou Prefecture is in a slump. Since the "Old Chuzhou Prefecture Highway Fundraising Committee" decided to collect 8% of the highway share payments from bamboo and wood charcoal merchants, and set up three branch offices in Suichang Beijie Town, Qu County Yangkou Town, and Qingyuan City, imitating the old system of Likin stations, to assess and collect the payments themselves, up to 32% or more, starting on April 16. The armed collection personnel of the Yangkou Second Branch Office seized a wood raft belonging to Wu Guanxiang, a boatman, containing more than 500 pieces of wooden boards and more than 200 pieces of rough sections, which was assessed by the office to be worth more than 60 yuan, and would be doubled if the deadline was exceeded. However, the price of the wood was only worth more than 200 yuan according to the Hangzhou market price. After this incident occurred, it aroused a strong reaction. Bamboo and wood charcoal merchants in the old Chuzhou Prefecture gathered in the Zhangshutan Suilong Wood Industry Association, Wenzhou Wood Industry Association, and other places to discuss and believe that the highway was originally a good policy, but the share payments should be borne jointly by the people of the entire prefecture. How can the bamboo and wood charcoal industry bear this heavy burden in the midst of this decline? Furthermore, the establishment of offices to collect payments is like Likin stations, which leads to more embezzlement and makes it difficult to collect road funds. Moreover, the Highway Committee violated the provincial order that payments should be collected from the owners and that 8% should be collected according to the selling price of rich land. After consultation, it was decided to send a telegram to the provincial government requesting it to consider the difficulties of the merchants and order the Old Chuzhou Prefecture Highway Committee to abolish the Likin-like method of collecting payments, and to notify all timber firms to stop paying payments, and to elect representatives Zhang Zhize, Cheng Zhenpeng, Zhou Shenfu, Zhang Tanghua, etc., to continue to appeal to the provincial government. The provincial government has approved the order to the Civil Affairs, Finance, and Construction Departments to investigate and verify the case separately. However, during this period, Director Wang of the Yangkou Second Branch Office has intensified his efforts and, during the mountain flood on the 9th of this month, suddenly fired guns to forcibly seize and detain nine wood rafts of Xinchang, Guangchang, Youji, and other firms, containing more than 20 pieces of fir wood, which were sailing in the rapids, and imprisoned five boatmen, Huang Fuji, Fuchen, Fugan, Fushen, Liao Changxiang, etc., in the office, ordering them to pay a fine of five yuan each. By the next morning, the wood rafts had drifted away and disappeared because no one was taking care of them. The boatmen were then released. Currently, each branch office is seizing rafts as soon as they see them, and merchants and people have stopped transporting goods. Bamboo and wood charcoal merchants in the old Chuzhou Prefecture are about to close down, and hundreds of thousands of workers who depend on this for a living are also in a state of semi-unemployment. At a time when the Red bandit Fang Zhimin's troops are invading the border of Zhejiang, if it triggers a popular uprising, it will be a great hidden worry for Zhejiang Province.

Tax Police Execute Four Deserters

Four soldiers from the 1st Regiment of the Kunshan Tax Police, Fang Guiqing, Yin Fu, Chen Ping, and Wu Qing, deserted from the camp with weapons. They were captured by the regiment headquarters and sent to the general headquarters for questioning. Fang and others confessed without denying. The general commander Wen Yingxing sentenced them to death in accordance with the Army, Navy, and Air Force Law and sent them back to the county for execution. At 10:00 AM on the 22nd, the regiment headquarters sent a platoon of soldiers to bring the four criminals back, and after the regiment commander Zhao verified their identities, they were escorted to the foot of Ma'anshan Mountain and executed by firing squad.

Yangzhou 100

Yang Senhe Leg Shop Sealed Up

The Yang Senhe Leg Shop has been open for many years and has accumulated assets of hundreds of thousands. In order to facilitate the scheduling of funds, it specifically added the Yonglong Money Shop, located in the Senhe store. Therefore, the two stores are not only fully invested in terms of assets, but also formally affiliated. Yang Yijiang is in charge of the affairs. Although it was established not long ago, it was able to attract local stores and absorb deposits due to the Senhe's strong capital. This spring, Yang Yijiang failed in speculative business, resulting in poor turnover and declared bankruptcy. The Senhe's main store, however, remained open as usual due to its deep roots and extremely wealthy family property. On the one hand, he entrusted Wang to handle the aftermath. Wang believed that the store was a famous wealthy household in the local area, and if it was not cleaned up, it would be difficult to quell public anger. Even with the current financial resources to clean up the Yonglong depositors, there would still be plenty to spare. Therefore, there was a proposal to repay 90%, which has been talked about for a long time, but has not yet been implemented. Most of the depositors, however, were unable to maintain their business or livelihood due to the impact of the Yonglong bankruptcy and had no choice but to litigate. As a result, the goods issued by Senhe were seized by the court, and the foreign port could not reach them. Yang Shaoquan, Yang Yijiang's uncle, a litigation trickster, was angered and spared no effort to expand the situation, insisting on recovering debts and repaying deposits, and canceling the original proposal to clear 90%. The court has ordered the seal to be issued because of repeated delays. It is now heard that the depositors are uniting and organizing groups. If there is still no clean-up plan after the Dragon Boat Festival, they will be forced to take further action.

Zhenjiang 101

Expansion of the Military Officer Training Class

The Jiangsu Provincial Security Department plans to establish a provincial military officer training class. The original plan has now been reorganized and expanded. The original internal organization was divided into four battalions and several platoons. Now, the number of battalions is not limited, and the special reorganization program has been submitted for record. Its organization is divided into ten battalions and more than twenty platoons. Trainees are designated as Grade A, B, and C: (A) Cadets, (B) Students, (C) Trainee Soldiers. The training period is still limited to six months. However, after graduating, Grade A cadets who pass the evaluation can be assigned to various counties to serve as company commanders. After graduating, Grade B students will be recommended by the institute to various military departments to serve as platoon leaders. After graduating, Grade C trainee soldiers will also be recommended by the institute to various military departments to serve as squad leaders. Trainee soldiers are selected from experienced soldiers recommended by the units under the jurisdiction of the department. Grade A, B, and C trainees are still recruited from public security officers dismissed from various counties. Everything is basically in place, and it is heard that recruitment may begin as early as mid-June.

Xiaoshan 104

Silkworm Rearing Failure, Hatred in Heart, Commits Suicide

Due to the uneven weather this year, the silkworm rearing in Dongxiang has been poor. On the 21st, the Xu family in Jiudun borrowed a large amount of silver dollars in advance for all the mulberry leaves for the local and foreign silkworms they were rearing. Unexpectedly, the thunderstorm changed the silkworm crop, and most of the local and foreign silkworms were lost. They were unable to repay the borrowed leaves. Now that the silkworms do not spin cocoons, they felt extreme hatred and went to Renshan Yiken Tree to commit suicide. His wife rushed to the scene after hearing the news, but he had already died.

The Fifth Batch of Relics Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 108

All 5,763 Boxes, Including the Dragon Throne of the Qianqing Palace, Are Also Transported

Guowen News Agency reports that the fifth batch of 5,851 boxes of antiquities from the National Palace Museum in Beiping, after arriving in Pukou, had 88 boxes of musical instruments from the Altar and Temple Management Office left in Nanjing to be moved to the Zhongshan Mausoleum. The other 5,763 boxes were loaded onto the China Merchants Bureau's Guangli wheel yesterday at 4:15 PM and transported to Shanghai. At that time, it docked at Pier No. 6 of Jinliyuan, and under the strict protection of the military police authorities of the Chinese and French Concessions and the capital military police escorting the goods to Shanghai, more than 400 boxes were unloaded first, and then stopped at about 7:00 PM to prepare for the continued unloading and storage in the warehouses at No. 26 Tianzhutang Street and No. 32 Sichuan Road today.

Public Report 109

When the Guangli wheel docked at the pier, the staff of the Palace Museum showed the reporters a report form with the following contents: (1) Antiquities: 2,412 boxes from the Palace Museum, 351 boxes from the Beiping Municipal Government's Summer Palace, and 3,000 boxes from the Ministry of Interior's Exhibition Hall, totaling 5,763 boxes to Shanghai. (2) Categories: Antiquities are books, paintings, bronzes, porcelain, and printed materials such as verification lists from the establishment of the museum. (3) Departure: The departure date from Beijing was 9:00 PM on May 22. (4) Supervision: Chen Rui, a counselor from the Executive Yuan, section chief Wang Jinliang, clerk Wang Hongxun, Zhai Zonghan, and six others. (5) Escort: Yu Tongkui, director of the General Affairs Department of the Palace Museum, Lu Xirong, director of the Ministry of Interior's Etiquette Department, Chuan Yiwen, director of antiquities preservation, and more than ten staff members. (6) The Capital Military Police Headquarters dispatched Adjutant Cai Xinya and Inspector Zhang Xing, leading a company of mixed soldiers drawn from the Second Regiment, carrying two machine guns for protection, and six other points.

Yu Tongkui Talks 110

The reporter then boarded the ship to meet with Yu Tongkui, director of the General Affairs Department of the Palace Museum, and asked for details. According to him, when the antiquities arrived in Pukou, only the Altar and Temple Management Office had 88 boxes of musical instruments, which were transported to the Zhongshan Mausoleum. Although the military situation in Beiping was tense, the area was still as quiet as usual when we left. There will be no more antiquities transported south in the future. As for the Jade Buddha in Tuancheng, it is made of stone and is not valuable, so it was decided not to transport it south temporarily. The throne of the Qianqing Palace (also known as the dragon chair) has now been brought along. Other miscellaneous antiquities are mostly calligraphy and painting. It is estimated that the total number of antiquities that have arrived in Shanghai, including these five batches, is over 19,000 boxes.

Anti-Dumping Duties to be Collected 111

Beginning Review of Goods Species

The Daily News reports that the two departments of finance and industry, in view of the dumping of foreign goods in China, which hinders the development of domestic goods, have specifically stipulated the collection of anti-dumping duties on foreign goods in order to maintain the operation of domestic goods. Before the anti-dumping duties are collected, a Foreign Goods Dumping Review Committee will be established to investigate the dumping of foreign goods in China. Yesterday, the Daily News reporter specifically inquired about everything from relevant parties, which is recorded as follows:

Collection Principle 112

In the past, when transportation was inconvenient in various countries, surplus goods in the country were often burned because they could not be transported. Today, world transportation is extremely convenient, and surplus goods can be dumped abroad. The purpose of dumping is only to get rid of the goods, regardless of profit or loss. Recently, factories in European and American countries have been affected by the economic panic and must maintain the lives of workers. Therefore, they have had to implement a dumping policy abroad. The principle of collecting anti-dumping duties is to collect duties on all dumped goods, while other promotional goods will not be taxed.

Establishment of Review Committee 113

The two departments of finance and industry believe that the collection of anti-dumping duties on foreign goods must start with the review of dumping types. Therefore, there is the organization of the Foreign Goods Dumping Review Committee. As for the candidates for its members, they are the Customs Administration, the National Tariff Commission of the Ministry of Finance, and the Agriculture Department, Industry Department, and Commerce Department of the Ministry of Industry, together with the International Trade Bureau, to organize the Review Committee.

Beginning of Review 114

The current Review Committee plans to investigate the dumping of foreign goods in China in Shanghai and other places first. It has recently started the investigation. However, the investigation is limited to the country, so it is impossible to fully understand whether a certain type of goods is dumped or promoted. Therefore, it has sent letters to consulates of various countries to investigate the prices of various goods nearby to determine whether they belong to dumping, and to collect tax rates when they are transported into Chinese ports.

Foreign Envoys Inquire 115

Since the two departments of finance and industry announced the news of the collection of anti-dumping duties on foreign goods, ministers from various countries have gone to the International Trade Bureau to inquire about the collection of anti-dumping duties on foreign goods. Yesterday morning around 10:00 AM, Hu Zan'er, commercial counselor of the Polish Embassy, and Don Elba, the Italian Consul General, went to the bureau to inquire about the collection methods and details, which were explained in detail by Ji Zejin, director of the Guidance Department.

British, Imperial, and Japanese Residents in England Celebrate Today 116

Today is British Empire Day, and all British residents around the world are celebrating to commemorate the creation of the empire. Therefore, it is one of the two greatest memorial days of the year, along with the King's birthday. The British residents in this port are still following the usual practice. At 7:45 AM, the Boy Scouts will be reviewed in the General Consulate Square, and the Acting Consul General Davis will give a brief speech to encourage the youth. At 8:00 AM, there will be a flag-raising ceremony. At 5:30 PM, there will be a military parade at the racecourse. In the evening, there will be a celebration banquet at the Capital Hotel.

The Great American Evening News reports that Gu Pu, general manager of the Associated Press, will arrive in Shanghai on June 6 aboard the Japanese Empress Wheel. Accompanying him will be Mrs. Gu Pu and Administrative Secretary Miss Gibbes. Gu Pu and others arrived in Yokohama on the 17th and are currently traveling in Japan. The Aid Association of Righteous Armies Notifies the Anti-Japanese Armies of Recent Situations 119

Requesting the Chengdu Chamber of Commerce to Provide Relief with the Collected Funds

The Northeast Righteous Armies Aid Association sent a letter to Mr. Wang Jianming, the president of the Chengdu Chamber of Commerce yesterday. It begins as follows: "To whom it may concern, the violent Japanese are invading and occupying our Northeast, attacking Rehe, crossing the Great Wall, and directly approaching Peiping and Tianjin. The survival of the country depends on the moment. To defend against insults and save the country, we rely on the loyal and brave anti-Japanese frontline troops. Recovering the lost land depends on the righteous and brave children lurking in the Northeast. Since September 18th, General Ma Zhanshan took the lead in raising the banner of righteousness. The armies in Liaoning and Jilin, such as Li Du, Feng Zhanhai, Wang Delin, Tang Juwu, and Zhu Jiqing, have successively risen to resist Japan, fought bloody battles for many years, and established numerous extraordinary achievements. However, due to the lack of relief and the exhaustion of aid, they retreated, which allowed the Japanese bandits to have no worries and turn to the interior. Sun Dianying and Song Zheyuan's armies have advanced without retreating and fought to the death, eliminating the Japanese bandits with their spirits. The world was shocked. In the end, due to insufficient support and many constraints, they could not launch a long-drive counterattack, which formed the current crisis. It is not that there are no armies in the country that are determined to resist Japan, but that they lack the support of real strength. Our association has been calling for assistance to the Northeast Righteous Armies and relief to the anti-Japanese soldiers for many years. We are ashamed of our meager strength and cannot universally benefit all armies. However, even a small amount of food and drink can boost morale. Today, the government's ability to resist has been exhausted. To save the crisis, we should pay more attention to the power of the people. We have long admired your association leaders for their enthusiasm in saving the country. We have recently learned that you have raised a large sum of money and have not yet determined its use. We dare to present our humble opinions and respectfully ask your association to consider the difficulties of the time and quickly allocate it for the relief of the following loyal and brave anti-Japanese armies and the aid to the Northeast Righteous Armies: (1) Song Zheyuan's army (preserved Xifengkou, annihilated two brigades of the Japanese army, Suzuki and Hattori, spared no sacrifice, and vowed to fight to the death); (2) Sun Dianying's army (fought in Rehexi, firmly defended the border of Chahar, vowed to coexist with the country and never retreat); (3) Huang Shouzhong's army (Huang is the leader of the Rehe militia, loved by the people of Rehe, recently recovered Rehexi, and is a threat to the enemy); (4) Wang Yizhe and Weng Zhaoyuan's army (Wang is the only anti-Japanese general in the Northeast Army who can fight. Weng is a brave general in the anti-Japanese battle in Shanghai and is now the commander of Wang's division, determined to resist Japan to the end); (5) Fang Zhenwu's army (Fang donated his property to pay the troops and is now leading his troops to Xuanhua to defend the border of Chahar); (6) Jilin Righteous Armies (the main troops are Wang Delin and Li Du's troops, totaling 50,000 people, occupying Antu, Dongning, Muling, Fuyuan, Raohe, Hulin, Mishan and other counties, now organized by Xiao Zhenying and Men Zhizhong, with the headquarters planning operations to recover the lost territory); (7) Heilongjiang Righteous Armies (after Su Ma left Heilongjiang Province, his subordinates Pu Bingshan and other righteous armies are no less than Jilin, now the association is actively contacting them to promote their launch). The Seafarers Guidance Committee Takes Over the Two Seafarers Unions 136

The Middle Cabin Public Association Opposes and Has Petitioned the Central Government

The Kuomintang Social Society and the Special Party Department of Chinese Seafarers, in order to reorganize the Shanghai Seafarers Union, sent members to take over the old union the day before yesterday, but were rejected and a conflict occurred. A part of the seafarers also petitioned the central government, which caused a dispute. Yesterday, the reporter specially inquired from all parties, which are recorded as follows:

Both Unions Send Members to Reorganize 137

It is found that there are more than 300,000 seafarers in Shanghai, and there are as many as 30 kinds of seafarers' organizations, with very complicated members. Since the Kuomintang took power, the Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Seafarers General Federation of Industry was established. Not long after, due to differences of opinion, a Maintenance Committee of the Shanghai Branch of the Seafarers was established, which was also approved by the Municipal Party Department (there was no Special Party Department of Seafarers at that time). Therefore, disputes arose from time to time. The Joint Office of the Nine Shipping Companies petitioned the Seafarers Party Department to reorganize it. The department sent seven people, including Chen Songnian, to form a temporary guidance committee and revoked the names of the two associations.

Conflict Occurs When Taking Over the Branch 138

After the seven committees received the order, they first went to Shenxiang Pavilion in Xinbeimen the day before yesterday to take over the documents and sundries of the Maintenance Committee, which were handed over without any problem. Then, they continued to take over the Shanghai Branch of the Seafarers in Danfeng Road, Xiaodongmen, but were rejected and petitioned the municipal government for protection in advance. The situation was serious at that time, and there was a slight conflict. Later, the guidance committee reported to the Party Department and transferred the Public Security Bureau to send police to suppress and armed takeover of a part. Yesterday morning, the handover of everything was continued, and it has now been completed and started working.

Talk from the Standing Committee of the Seafarers Party Department 139

According to Yu Jiayong, Standing Committee Member of the Special Party Department of Seafarers, the reorganization of the Seafarers Union this time is to guide the provisional measures for people's groups in accordance with the central government's regulations, and to comply with the requests of various seafarers' groups. The reception had some problems because it was bewitched by a few elements. Now the reception has been completed. Since its establishment, the Headquarters has been working hard to improve the seafarers' movement. The Seafarers Union has been reorganized into a temporary guidance committee in Qingdao, Fuzhou and Shanghai. Other South China lines and Yangtze River lines have also sent people to investigate. In the future, according to the organizational rules, a branch will be set up on each ship, a branch will be set up on important river banks, and a general union will be set up nationwide.

Some Seafarers Oppose Reorganization 140

Some seafarers in the Seafarers Middle Cabin Public Association believe that the reorganization of the Seafarers Union by the Seafarers Party Department this time is an illegal act. Because the Seafarers Union is directly under the Central People's Movement Committee and is handled directly by the central government, the department has no right to reorganize it, and the guidance committees sent are not seafarers and cannot be recognized. Therefore, representatives such as Wang Shenxiu have been promoted and went to Beijing yesterday morning to petition the Central People's Movement Committee to stop the illegal actions of the Party Department.

The Ministry of Communications Orders the Modification of Telegraph Receiving and Sending Methods 142

The Shanghai Wireless Telegraph Main Station of the Ministry of Communications at the Old North Gate in this city received an order from the ministry yesterday regarding Article 35 of the Telegraph Receiving and Sending Methods, which stipulates that a special delivery fee should be charged for delivering telegrams to recipients whose addresses are more than five li away from the station. In order to give preferential treatment to the recipients, telegrams will be delivered in the future, and no special delivery fee will be charged regardless of the distance if the recipient's address is within the same city as the station. It is heard that the modified article is as follows: "If the address of the recipient of a telegram delivered by a telegraph office or wireless telegraph station is within the same city as the station, no special delivery fee will be charged. If it is not in the same city, no special delivery fee will be charged within five li of the station. From five li to ten li, 15 cents will be charged. From ten li to fifty li, an additional 15 cents will be charged for every ten li. Beyond fifty li, an additional 20 cents will be charged for every ten li. For example, 95 cents should be charged for sixty li, and so on. For distances beyond ten li, the remainder of less than ten li will also be calculated according to ten li."

Methods for Importing Opium Powder 144
